RussIAN FEDERATION
AGRICULTURAL REFORM IMPLEMENTATION SUPPORT (ARIS) PROJECT
MARKET INFRASTRUCTURE DEVELOPMENT
SUB-SECOR BACKGROUND
1.    Price liberalization and privatization of marketing organizations have been the key elements of
the Russian Government's economic reform program. Since 1992, the Federal Government took
significant initiatives to liberalize prices for a majority of agricultural commodities (inputs and outputs);
reduce formal procurement quotas; allow non-government agencies to buy and sell agricultural produce
in the open market; and break up monopolies. Market-based transactions by producers, traders and
consumers are rapidly expanding. However, broad-based market development could be much faster, had
it not been constrained by the lack of necessary policy and legal framework, institutions and physical
infrastructure.
2.    Future reforms need to focus on redefining the role of MOAF and other federal and local
agencies with regard to agricultural marketing and market development. Institutional limitations include
the lack of adequate retail and wholesale market facilities, a market information system and a
comprehensive system of grades aind standards that will help determine product prices by quality. The
absence of modern storage, packaging, transportation facilities, labeling and containerization have helped
perpetuate the existence of monopolistic institutions of the former command economy.
3.    The main thrust of the proposed project will, therefore, be to provide substantial technical
assistance and training to MOAF and local governments to define their catalytic role in market
development; strengthen their organizations to perform this new role efficiently; and establish legal,
institutional and operational framework for emerging primary and wholesale markets and commodity
exchanges for agricultural products. Concurrently, the project will assist the establishment of a
nationwide market information system and finance few pilot investments to demonstrate systemic and
institutional reforms that should be introduced to promate the development of agricultural marketing.
MARKET INFORMATION SYSTM
The Present System
4.    Russia's prevailing institutional arrangements for collection and dissemination of agricultural
market information have been designed primarily to serve the needs of a command economy. Despite
some improvements, following partial liberalization of the economy, significant gaps remain in the
timeliness, and the range and depth of market information that is available to agricultural producers,
traders, processors, consumers and policy makers.



66                                   ANNEx
Page 2 of 10
5.    Currently, two main agencies are involved in the collection of economic and market information.
These are the State Committee on Statistics (Goskomstat) and MOAF. None of these agencies have
systems which could efficiently serve expanding need for market information. Price information
disseminated by various other agencies and institutions is derived mainly from Goskomstat and MOAF
sources and is supplemented by information provided by commodity exchanges. Goskomstat is not
geared for providing price information on a day-to-day basis. Under the project, MIS will use
Goskomstat; help rationalize its data collection and processing methodologies; and avoid unproductive
and costly overlap in Goskomstat and MOAF activities.
MIS Design
6.    Information flows for the proposed MIS are indicated in Annex Figure 3.1. Information will flow
primarily from rayon offices to oblast offices. Oblast offices will also collect and process local
information and manage the database. Central MIS office at Moscow will draw information from
databases at the oblast level, commodity exchanges, Goskomstat and international databases.
Computer System Design
7.    The computer system will be designed to support the requirements of the overall ARIS project.
This includes Market Information System (MIS), Farmer Information and Advisory Services (FIAS) and
Seed Industry Development (SID). Only MIS and FIAS components of the ARIS project have been
evaluated at this time. The computer system design will utilize the latest hardware and software
technology. RISC based computer systems using UNIX operating systems and the Distributed Computing
Environment (DCE) for the servers have been selected for the computer system design. This design has
several advantages: (i) it is possible to use multiple vendors; (ii) it will proviJe for a wider selection of
peripherals and supporting software; and (iii) it has built-in flexibility for future inclusion of new
hardware technologies without the need to replace or upgrade existing computers or communications
equipment. Network-wide security will be an integral part of the design. The design of the computer
system is based on three tiers of information processing:
o     Rayon Level: The first and smallest of these tiers at the rayon level provide the primary
collection and dissemination points for all information to the farmers. Because the users
of this network have widely varying capabilities, multiple methods of communicating the
information have been included in the design.
•     Oblast Level: Information collected from farmers and processing plants located in each
rayon is forwarded to the oblast centers for processing and consolidation with input from
other rayons. The consolidated information is then sent back to the rayons for their use.
O     Federal Level: Oblast data is forwarded to the Federal Center for final consolidation and
for broadcast back to the oblasts and rayons and to press, radio and television
organizations for public dissemination.
Design Overview
8.    The principle design criteria for the ARIS computer system are: (i) ease of use; (ii) best available
contemporary technology; (iii) ease of expansion and reconfiguration; (iv) security of high value data;



67                                  ANNEX 3
Page 3 of 10
(v) effective use of available communication facilities and bandwidth; (vi) integration with existing
international and domestic services; (vii) rapid implementation. To meet these requirements, the ARIS
computer systems design will be a distributed object network where all users have access to all
information within the constraints of their authorization. Advanced software technology created by the
Oren Software Foundation (OSF) known as the Distributed Computing Environment (DCE) technology
was selected as the common framework across all computers located in the network. A user can be
granted access to any information on a selective basis. If access is not granted, that information will be
excluded from the user's processing view. To meet the need to interface ARIS with other international
and domestic networks, the Federal server provides all ARIS users an interface to the Internet and to
multiple commodity networks.
Computer Network Topology
9.    The ARIS computer network is designed to be expanded over the next five years to more than
1500 nodes (addressable computers) networked together as a distributed computing system. Each location
with the computer system may have access to one or both of the existing X.25 packet net'.orks. The
network provides communications circuits between any two computers (nodes) upon request but,
normally, little information will move directly between the end Lisers. End users are clustered and
supported by a single rayon processing facility, which, in turn, is clustered with other rayons within a
single oblast. Normally, most of the information will flow from the end user to the assigned rayon's
location and then to its associated oblast processing center. Each oblast will have a powerful server that
will consolidate and process all of the data received from the geographically dispersed rayons. This
consolidated information will be made available to the Federal server for additional consolidation and
processing. The consolidated data will be supplied to the Russian radio, TV and print media. The
Federal data will also be passed back to all oblasts for distribution back to the rayons and ultimately to
the end users.
10.   Applications developed for the ARIS project will consist of both off-the-shelf personal
productivity packages and applications custom built for commodity information collection, consolidation
and distribution. All applications, regardless of their source, will be integrated into a single, consistent
graphical interface. The user will only have to learn a single way to accomplish almost all tasks. As an
example, entry of text will be the same for E-Mail as for a letter. Numerical information will be the
same for a spreadsheet as for collection of commodity prices. Any information created will be available
for use by all applications without error-prone data conversions.
Telecommunications
11.   There are three major interrelated problems with the telecom infrastructure in the Russian
Federation at the present time: (i) there are insufficient telephone mainlines and telephones; (ii) the
telephone switching and transmission network is inadequate, resulting in many failed attempts; and (iii)
when a connection is completed, the transmission quality, even in Moscow, is usually very poor.
Although the teletypewriter system of telecommunication service is being phased out in Western
Countries, it operates very well in the Russian Federation and is widely used. The most common and
preferred way of connecting computers for most applications is the X.25 Packet Switching Service.
Coverage of oblast and some rayon seats by at least two carriers was quite good and growing. Moreover,
the real problem with the service appears to be underutilization, which is a pleasant problem from the
computer user's viewpoint. Radio Telephone Service offers another means for reaching end-users, i.e.,



68                                      _
Page 4 of 10
users located outside oblast and rayon seats. There are agricultural areas in Russia where a user may be
an hour's drive or more from the nearest telephone. The ITU report estimates that in 1991, 36,000 rural
settlements had no access to a telephone. The report goes on to say that newer technologies, notably
satellite and radio-based commnunications, could alleviate the problem but the issue of who pays remains
unsolved. Cellular telephones are clearly not the right solution as they require far greater densities of
use than what is needed for this project. Locally developed radio systems that can connect about 35
subscribers to a base station at a cost of less than US$20,000 exist. It is a very cost-effective solution
in many situations and is being tried out as a pilot in this project.
12.   The MIS and FIAS systems will have similar telecom topologies. The telecom subsystem design
should be independent of whether the two systems share computers or locations. The objectives of the
MIS/FIAS telecom subsystem will be: (i) effectiveness (i.e., ability to do the job for which it is designed;
(ii) efficiency, including low cost; (iii) flexibility, including independence of any rules regarding data flow
and ease of adding new computer centers; (iv) low error rate; (v) single data entry; and (vi)
Reliability/Uptime. The MIS/FIAS telecom subsystem will make use of the existing and planned telecom
infrastructure, the expansion of which is not within the scope of this project.
13.   A number of alternative telecommunication solutions varying in terms of practicability,
effectiveness and cost were reviewed and evaluated by the appraisal mission and the conclusion was
reached that the best alternative was the use of the X.25 packet switching network. At present, there are
two reasonably well deployed packet switching networks that serve many of the proposed MIS/FIAS
locations (i.e., oblast and rayon seats). Both the MOT ROSPAC network and SPRINT NETWORKS are
operational. By the beginning of 1994, the ROSPAC network will have switching nodes in 64 oblast
centers and 27 rayon centers. SPRINT -with 31 current locations-has somewhat smaller coverage, but
has formed partnerships with several regional networks. There are also other providers of X.25 services.
All of the providers have plans for expanding their networks. In the short run, the rayon level MIS and
FIAS sections will make use of available telecommunication systems, including telefax and mailing
diskettes. MOAF's computer center, in association with MOT, will be responsible for establishing the
most efficient telecommunication network in each oblast and rayon.
Computer System Organization
14.   MOAFCC is being reorganized to meet the needs of the computer systems for the MIS and FPAS
components. The new MOAFCC management structure will reflect the distributed nature of the computer
network on which it is built. The MOAFCC at the federal level will direct the day-to-day operations,
plan initial installations and upgrades, create future plans, conduct or arrange for all of the user and
technical training and interface to the functional organizations. MIS and FIAS would view the MOAFCC
as the computer and network services provider. Each facility at the rayon and oblast levels will have
local management primarily responsible for the operation of the MIS and FIAS components. The oblast
management will have responsibility for a majority of the network's daytime activities and the
MOAFCC assuming overall responsibility after normal business hours. The new organizational structure
(see Annex Figure 3.2) will consist of four divisions, viz. operations, design and architecture, training
and application development.



69                                   ANNEX 3
Page 5 of 10
PILT INVESTMENTS IN MARKET DEVELOPMENT
15.   The project will finance pilot investments to demonstrate systemic and institutional reforms that
should be introduced to promote development of agricultural marketing. MOAF, in consultation with
local governments, suggested three administrative units for the ARIS project: Moscow City, Moscow
Oblast and Belgorod Oblast. The project emphasis is on developing marketing systems for fruit and
vegetables as this sub-Fector has been substantially liberalized, unlike grain and livestock products. Some
25 sub-projects were identified and reviewed by technical experts on the Bank Preparation and Appraisal
missions. Likely sub-projects are identified in Table Annex Tables 3.1-3.3 though additional sub-projects
which are consistent with the project concept could be included during project implementation, if such
investments provide satisfactory financial and economic rates of returns and the borrowing enterprises
satisfy eligibility criteria.
16.   It is important to emphasize that the proposed project is not intended to meet even a small part
of the prevailing demand for investment funds which must be increasingly met by addressing current
market failures and price distortions and strengthening the commercial banking system which can provide
longer term credit to enterprises. The technical consultants on Bank missions have made inportant
recommendations on designs and layouts and choice of technology. This analysis indicated that if the
Bank must finance market investments, it is important to analyze the status of the total marketing chain -
- from production to retailing and require enterprises to address related constraints as to ensure the
financial feasibility of the investments. Currently, the productivity and product quality at most
enterprises, especially in potato and vegetables, is poor and must be substantially improved. The post-
harvest technology is also outdated causing considerable losses to producers. Although cold storages for
cabbage and other seasonal vegetables are expected to be viable with current levels of productivity and
product quality, the project provides for technical assistance to participating farms for introduction of new
varieties which could be stored for longer times and contribute to productivity improvements. Substantial
improvements can be made by restructuring production by relocating production on lands which are
suitable for potato, by introducing new varieties that are suitable for long-term storage; and by providing
modern post-harvest facilities. The project will, therefore, finance on a pilot basis, only the renovation
of existing potato storages to improve their efficiency.

RussIAN FEDERATIoN
AGRiCULTURAL REFORM MPLEMENTATION SUPPORT (ARIES) PROJECT
FARMER INFORMWTION AND ADvISORY SERVICE
INFORMATION SYS1EM IN THE PASr
1.    In the past, the information system in virtually all sectors was strictly state controlled and was
essentially designed to meet the requirements of centralized planning. The system offered limited
opportunities for meeting the information needs, especially those of the agricultural producers, at the
grass roots level. This resulted in the development of specialists in large state and collective farms. These
specialists served as in-house specialists in addressing a variety of crop and livestock related problems.
This was supplemented by research and field applications through a wide network of a variety of
agricultural research institutes and experimental stations. Most of the research results were introduced
through directives, with few incentives to promote new innovations.
2.    Although the education and training system in the Russian Federation was designed to meet the
requirements of a socialistic economy, the most positive outcome was its contribution to making the
Russian Federation obtain one of the highest literacy rates in the world. Despite the significant structural
reforms initiated since December 1991, not much progress has been made to educate the people on basic
principles of market economics, standard business practices and to develop an appropriate information
system, which is freely accessible to those who desire to use it. This is particularly important in the
context of the many forms of newly emerging farm structures.
3.    Information services for farms and farmers were an integral part of the former centralized system
of information services. Very little information sourcing, message development or media packaging took
place at the local level. Data was channeled to Moscow where information packages, based on a central
assessment of local needs, were developed and transmitted from the center directly to the state and
collective farms, primarily via dense print publications. Radio, TV and, to some extent, computers were
used as dissemination mechanisms. The channels by which farms and farmers have been receiving
information were few and there were no avenues for cross-checking the information received. The
centralized system was primarily aimed at meeting production targets.
INFORMATION SYSITM IN THE PRESET
4.    The break-up of the former Soviet Union and break-down in administrative structures has created
a widening "infonmation gap" to all types of agricultural producers. The present budgetary problems,
and the resulting shortage of resources, has sharply curtailed the government's ability to meet the growing
demand for basic information to agricultural producers. Developing information packages that are
responsive to local perceptions and needs will entail a reorientation of those involved in the information
development and dissemination. The main goal of the Farmer Information and Advisory Services
component, therefore, is to provide the most critical information support services needed to bridge this



76                                   AMA 4
Page 2 of 7
"information gap" and enable the new types of emerging farm organizations to transform to a market
economy.
PROJECr CONCEPr: NED BASED 4-M MODUL4R APPROACH
5.    The underlying concept of this component is need based Multi-source, Multi-user, Multi-
disciplinary and Multimedia approach (hereafter referred to as the 4-M modular approach). This concept
has been illustrated in Annex Figure 4.1. It consis.s of the following four steps: (i) participatory
diagnostic information needs assessment; (ii) development of information packages; (iii) multi-Media
Information dissemination; and (iv) feedback mechanisms.
6.    The FIAS component is based on the development of existing institutions, availability of an
extensive network of agricultural research institutes, laboratories and chemical stations, land data banks,
academies and universities, a highly skilled labor force and provides for flexibility to incorporate rapidly
evolving changes in the information technology environment. It also takes into consideration the available
communication infrastructure, logistic problems associated with a dispersed farm population and local
technological and resource constraints.
Partiipatory diagnosc information needs .;essment
7.    The first step is to assess the end-user's information needs. A wide range of agricultural clientele
would be the target group and it would encompass all types of restructured farms, individual farmers,
agro-processing enterprises, household gardeners and agricultural related public. A participatory process,
directly involving the various end-users to define and prioritize their information needs, will be used.
This process would assist in the assessment of the demand for information, local problems, constraints
and the expectations of the various users from the information system.
8.    In this regard, the All Russian Scientific and Research Institute of Innovation and Management
in Agriculture (ARSRIIMA) has already carried out a comprehensive multi-user information needs survey
in 36 rayons in 12 regions (Kemerovo, Kostroma, Lipetsk, Nizhny Novgorod, Rostov, Ryazan, Vladimir,
Voronezh, Tambov, Krasnodar, Bashkortostan and Tartarstan). The respondents were frmn households,
joint stock companies, collective fArms, state farms, partnerships and individual farmers. Over 5000
types of information on various types of agricultural activity was obtained. Based on the response, the
following specific areas of information needs were identified:
o     Priority One: Legal and financial information, especially pertaining to changing laws on
privatization and land; credit availability, banking and taxation issues, how to set up a
farm business, farm management techniques and principles of market accounting;
*     Priority Two: Methods of processing of agricultural products, especially milk and meat;
O     Priority 7hree: Information on various aspects of mechanization, with special reference
to mini-machinery, mini-production lines, complex mechanization for grain production,
mobile harvesters, small tractors and general agricultural machinery;
O     Priority Four: Application of new veterinary medicines and its availability, especially
with reference to poultry, fur-bearing animals, fish and bees.



77                                     ANNEX 4
Page 3 of 7
9.    The development of multi-disciplinary information packages will be based on the results of an
on-going client information needs assessment process. That process would systematically combine
recording specific requests from individual farmers with the results of interactive needs assessment
forums.  In the context of these forums, outside specialists representing national and international
perspectives engage a selected group of farmers from the region in an interactive dialogue where new
ideas from the outside are exchanged with the local farmer viewpoints to create an ever-evolving
prioritization of farmer information needs. As this is a key step, which would determine the success of
the FIAS component, the project will introduce modern tested methods for determining what types of
infornation various clients want, in what detail and willingness to pay for this service. It will also provide
facilitator training for FIAS staff in the dynamics of multi-stakeholder consensus building processes.
Development of information packages
10.   The second step involves the development of client and media specific multi-disciplinary
information packages from a variety of sources.
11.   Sources of Information: There are a number of scientific and research institutes operating in the
Russian Federation, which cater to various types of agricultural data needs. Broadly, there are two
academies, 249 agricultural scientific and research institutes, various independent institutes and
universities. Given the broad range of available source of information, the FIAS component would
initially focus on those sources which are suited to providing the information in greatest demand by the
various users. This makes the needs assessment aspect of the project extremely important. Some of the
potential sources infonnation are provided below.
12.   Russian Acadeny of Agricultural Sciences (RAAS): The main institution in agricultural research
is the RAAS, founded in early 1992, as thz successor to its previous Soviet counterpart, to assume apex
responsibility for infrastructure, staff and programs. Increasingly, the MOAF is assuming a larger share
of this responsibility, and may be poised to respond more quickly to the demands of reform. Also, the
Ministry of Science, Higher Education and Technology Policy (MOS) contributes to agricultural research,
mainly through its policy-setting and funding influence over RAAS, and its conduct of basic scientific
research, for example, on biogenetics and nuclear energy.
13.   RAAS also coordinates agro-industrial research, provides training of scientific personnel and
maintains professional links with foreign countries. Under its umbrella, RAAS administers a variety of
support institutions, ranging from design offices, research institutes and experiment stations to state
experimental farms, agro-processing and seed factories. Facilities within the RAAS structure are also
the primary suppliers of crop production inputs, such as basic seeds and pedigree livestock. Associated
with these institutions and facilities are numerous personnel and vast tracts of land. As the agricultural
research and higher education enterprise, integrated and coupled to the broadened concept of extension,
breaks out of previously rigid structures of being funded and operated, new ways of doing research,
training and servicing new clients and new sources of funding are likely to emerge.
14.   Regional scientific research institutes: Scientific research on the various aspects of wheat
production is the responsibility of 16 selection and production centers, located in various regional
scientific research institutes. These institutes deal with the creation of varieties, provide agronomic
recommendations specific to local soil, climate and environmental conditions. This on-going research
is carried out under the broad umbrella of tie All Russian Scientific and Technical Program, "Grain and



78                                   ANNEX 4
Page 4 of 7
Grain Products", State Scientific and Technical Programn called "Perspective Agricultural Production
Processes". The research is also coordinated with oth;,. International Research Institutes, such as
ICARDA in Syria, CIMMYT in Mexico and ICRISAT in India. Research in oilseed crops, to provide
another example, is being carried out by the All Russian Scientific Institute for oilseed crops which has
active cooperation with various selection centers in other countries, such as Cargill Enterprises, USA,
Institute of Field Crops and Vegetables in Novi Sad, Institute of Sunflower and Wheat in Yugoslavia,
Institute of Selection and Acclimatization of Plants in Poland and the Research Institute of Grain and
Technical Crops in Romania. Another important crop, which is grown mostly by the private sector, is
potatoes whose research on 107 potato varieties is carried out by the All Russian Scientific and Research
Institute of potato growing which has research centers spread out all over the country. Similar research
is being carried out for other important grains, such as rye, barley, maize, oats and oilseed crops.
15.   Academies as sources of information: The most important agricultural academy is the Tinmryazev
Academy, which is the oldest and most prestigious agricultural educational institution in the Russian
Federation. Over the last 25 years, it has trained about 20,000 agronomists, agricultural chemists,
livestock specialists, economists and 7000 teachers for secondary agricultural educational schools. It
produces a variety of manuals on various agricultural aspects which is widely used.
16.   Management Institutes: A vatiety of technical and management institutes have emerged focussing
on providing training and developing a range of specialized materials needed for preparing basic farm
business plans, evolving market strategies, evaluation of business alternatives and financial analysis.
17.   Development of multi-disciplinary information packages: The rayon and oblast level FLAS
centers will be the primary contact points for the provision of farmer information. These centers would
provide agricultural advisory services and serve as the primary source of agricultural information. Trained
specialists in these centers would have access to a variety of information, agricultural packages and
databases made available through the electronic network. These centers would also have a variety of
locally developed and international materials related to various aspect of agriculture. Close coordination
will be maintained with the MIS centers. In situations where the rayon level specialists are unable to
provide the required information, these will be channeled to the oblast information development centers
and the Federal FIAS center, where staff would research a range of local, national and international
sources for relevant material. FIAS staff would be trained in how to source for material relevant to a
particular information need using various techniques, including the use of electronic clearinghouses and
databases.
18.   During the first few months of project implementation, the emphasis would be on the development
of very basic information packages as follows: (i) principles of farm management; (ii) essentials of farm
business planning; (iii) current land reform regulations; (iv) how to obtain credit; (v) environmental
regulations; (vi) technical advice on selected critical farm problems; (vii) do's and don'ts of basic fanning
practices; and (viii) basic market information on crops, livestock and inputs.
19.   The most important design criteria for the development of the basic farmer information packages
is simplicity, both in comprehension and language in order for it to be effective and useful. Due to the
lack of appropriate terminology of some critical Western concepts of business and economics in the
Russian language, new terms, which can be easily understood by the farmer, may have to be created in
Russian.



79                                  ANNEX 4
Page 5 of 7
20.   Multi-Media Information Packaging: The specialized information would be translated into
everyday terms familiar to each target audience and present it in a format that makes common sense and
has immediate practical value. The project will focus on skill enhancements that will demonstrate how
the agricultural user can employ an array of media strategies to increase his exposure to a wide range of
choices.  These approaches will be developed and tested. Methodologies will be extended to the
expanding national program once the innovations and new technologies involved have been refined, tested
and evaluated to assess impact, cost effectiveness and adaptability to other oblasts.
Multi-Media Information Dissemination
21.   Dissemination of information packages will be coordinated through the FIAS centers. A variety
of media would be used to channel farmer information to multiple users. This will include television,
video, print, radio, agricultural fairs and exhibitions and computer. The FIAS staff will be trained in
distributing messages into a multimedia package. They will be trained to ascertain which components
of the message are more appropriate for radio, video, print and computer diskette. Once the various
aspects of the message are assigned to specific media, the FIAS center will then sub-contract its media
package to particular media-production agencies, coordinating the development of the overall package.
22.   Some information needs are expected to reflect local conditions while others are expected to
emerge simultaneously in various parts of the country reflecting concerns common in all parts of the
country. These more general concerns will be referred by the projects coordinating body, where
appropriate, to national media outlets as the basis for the development of national mass media information
packages. These too may involve the coordinated development of video/TV, radio, print and computer-
based information products in order to effectively respond to the particular need identified.
23.   Video Productions: MOA'S Video Center. The MOAF currertly has a video unit in Moscow. Its
main function is to provide support for press conferences and serve as a media outlet for visiting
delegations, agreement ceremonies and coverage of important agricultural events. The project will assist
the MOAF in the establishment of national and international agricultural video library in Moscow. As
the video unit has tremendous potential to contribute to farmer information services, the FIAS component
would support the production and dissemination of a number of video programs. The proposed video
productions during the first project year are: (i) improved agricultural techniques; (ii) organization and
delivery of agricultural services; (iii) appropriate technologies for planting grain, fodder crops and
vegetables; (iv) st6ring techniques for various agricultural commodities; (v) intensive technologies for
animal breeding; and (vi) veterinary provision and animal care. AKKOR Video Center: The projects
support for AKKOR video center would enable it to produce a variety of productions aimed at the
infonnation needs of the private farmer. These would include: (i) mini sketches of life in the private
farm - problems and solutions; (ii) new farmers and their development; (iii) world experiences of farmers
and relating to local needs; (iv) programs for the private farner; and (v) exchange farmer. The video
productions are also expected to be aired in national television.
24.   Print Publications: Print publications will be divided between the AKKOR publications and
publications developed by the federal FIAS center and will be printed through the existing facilities at the
MOAF or through contractual services. Those infornation packages targeting newly independent family
farmers will be distributed through AKKOR while those targeting specialists and the reorganized state
and collective farms will be distributed through the FIAS federal center. Print productions are expected
to concentrate on center spreads or inserts to national, regional and local newspapers related to the



80                                   ANNEX 4
Page 6 of 7
information packages being developed by the information centers of those areas. These would provide
farmer oriented newspapers, brochures, pamphlets in a form which is user friendly and of immediate
relevance to meeting the information needs of private farmers and agri-business enterprises.
25.   Training will be provided to ensure that print productions become engaging to the FIAS client
groups, rather than a continuation of the old pattern of dense print journals laden with technical jargon.
Pages will be developed with generous open spaces, graphics, photos, symbols and other non-print visual
imagery while the text itself will incorporate subtitles, columns, featured quotes, black/white reversals,
section divisions and controlled vocabulary.
26.   Because of the number of different organizations producing print material of relevance to specific
agricultural client groups, the project will establish an electronic document clearinghouse that will
catalogue all the documents available on a given topic with a brief description to facilitate search and find.
A stock of the key documents will be maintained with fax back and mail services for servicing client
group requests.
27.   Computer: The use of computers, as a means of obtaining a variety of information, is expected
to increase over the next few years. The establishment of the necessary electronic infrastructure would
provide a critically needed support service. Initially, as the use of computers is expected to be slow, the
focus will be on training and the development of appropriate agricultural data bases in selected oblasts
and rayons. Based on the experience gained, and the response of the clients, dissemination of information
through the electronic media will be developed.
Update through feedback mechanism
28.   The changing needs of the various clients requires frequent updating of information in a variety
of areas, most notably on various agricultural reforms, liberalization measures, price and subsidy policies
and the problems faced by the emerging private farmers and enterprises. The FIAS component
incorporates a feedback mechanism, which will use tested modern methods, in order to adapt the
information development, packaging and its dissemination to suit the client needs.

RUssIAN FEDERATION
AGRICULTURAL REFORM IPLEMENTATION SUPPORT (APS) PROJECT
SEED INDUSTRY DEVELOPMENT
IN1ODUCrION
1.    Although Russia has the potential to produce all the required seed domestically, processing units
with up-to-9 -te technology, manag.-ment skills to produce seeds of international standard and required
policy environment for commercial seed industry are lacking. Demand for high quality seed is strong
and expected to expand but remains largely unsatisfied. MOAF continues to perform its pre-reform role:
allocating seed targets to oblasts' governments/farms; fixing seed prices; administering seed subsidies;
and directing distribution of seed. For the Russian seed industry to change from the state system to a
commercial system, it is essential to provide the necessary institutional and policy framework for efficient
functioning of private seed enterprises. Increasingly, seed production and marketing decisions must be
taken by seed growers, processors, and traders in response to market demand. The govenmment has to
encourage establishment of commercial seed enterprises in the private sector and provide necessary
support to market oriented seed industry in terms of varietal improvement, quality control, and setting
up of certification standards. This is the main theme of the seed industty development component of this
project.
REcENT INATIVES To PRIVATZE THE SEED INDUSIRY
2.    The government has taken a few, but important, initiatives towards establishing a competitive seed
industry through: (i) privatization: by Decree No. 708, dated September 4, 1992, the Government has
initiated privatization of all enterprises including seed enterprises and sovkhozes and kolkhozes
specializing in seed production; (ii) elimination of pice ceiling: elimination of price ceilings on hybrid
corn seed and oilseeds including sunflower, to encourage private seed production and competitive
marketing; and (iii) protection ofplant breeders'rights: enactment of law in August 1993 to protect plant
breeders' rights.
3.    The Russian seed inlustry is regulated by: (i) the State Commission for Varietal Testing
(Gosortkomissia) which requires .ompulsory registration of all seed varieties by the Variety Testing
Service (ii) the State Seed Inspection System (Gosseminspektsia) for quality control which ensures seed
inspection, certification and labelling of seeds supported by seed testing laboratories; and (iii) a plant
quarantine system which ensures prevention of plant pests and diseases through imports of pest and
disease free planting materials.
SED PRICING POuCY
4.    The government policy to administer seed prices has consistently reduced incentives to produce
high quality seeds and has contributed to reduced levels of investments in seed industry. For example,



83                                  ANNEX 5
Page 2 of 9
the corn seed price was determined by a formula of administered grain price plus a certain percentage
for varietal quality for seed multiplication (usually 700% of grain price fixed for hybrid corn)+25% of
costs for corn seed processing. This pricing formula demonstrated to the enterprises that higher profits
can be attained not by efficiency enhancement but by increased costs. [ ow prices of seed raise serious
questions about the financial viability of investments in seed industry though such investments could be
justified on economic grounds, as increased production of quality seeds will lead to import substitution.
However, this project requires and the government has agreed to liberalize hybrid corn and sunflower
seed prices and to eliminate seed subsidies for the imported and domestic seeds for these crops.
WHY CORN AND SUNFOWER SEEDS?
5.    Russia's annual imports of grain, over the last few years, has been around 20 million tons, 40%
of which has been corn, worth about US$1 billion. Further, around 40,000 tons of corn seeds are
imported, valued at over US $ 60 million annually to meet the domestic demand for corn grain and silage
production. Corn area in Russia has averaged around 11 nillion ha (1986-1991): about 1.4 million ha
under grain and the balance (9.7 million ha) under silage. The demand for com seed is estimated to be
around 450,000 tons. Until recently, the major area of corn seed production in FSU was in Ukraine and
Moldova. Following the break-up of FSU, this supply source has been disrupted. Corn seed availability
within Russia is now limited to 240,000 tons. Corn grain yields are around 3.0 to 3.8 tons per ha
(average in 1988-92 was 3.16 tons) although potential yields could be 6 to 10 tons. In the case of
sunflower, yields have been around 0.8 to 1.6 tons (the average in 1988- 92 was 1.33 tons). These yields
can be increased to 2.5 to 3 tons/ba by improving quality of seeds. Farms are convinced that when a
good quality hybrid seeds are used, the productivity improves dramatically.
6.    Sunflower is an important source of vegetable oil in Russia. Demand for vegetable oil in Russia
is about 2.5 million tons. Annual Russian imports are around 600,000 tons of vegetable oil, worth US
$ 275 million and oilseed meal worth US$ 500 million. During 1992, about 850 tons of sunflower seeds
were imported at a cost of US $ 3.7 million. Area under sunflower varies betwveen 2.8 to 3.1 million
ha, with a production range of 2.9 to 3.4 million tons. Area under sunflower is increasing rapidly. It
has increased form 2.1 million ha in 1987 to 2.9 million ha in 1992. The yield varies between 0.6 to
1.2 tons per ha. Only 10% of the area is covered with hybrids. There is potertial for development and
production of high quality seeds of hybrid sunflower. This will improve genetic quality of the seeds used
in the traditional area of Central Chernozome and Volga Valley. Nearly 40% yield increase can be
attained by using good quality hybrid sunflower seeds. Enhancing the quality and quantity of hybrid
sunflower seeds can enhance production, improve vegetable oil availability and save foreign exchange.
The project, therefore, supports Government effort to enhance the production of quality hybrid seeds of
corn and sunflower.
EXIsG SE) PRODUCrlON AND PROCESSING SYsm
7.    Russian hybrid corn and sunflower seeds production structure includes two tier system. (i)
experimental farms of research institutes - which produce elite and primary seeds of inbred lines (A and
B, male and female parents of hybrids); (ii) specialized seed farms (semkhozes)which produce seeds of
single or double cross hybrids. Increasingly, parent seed lines of these crops are produced, processed and
distributed by Scientific Production Unions called "Nauchno Proizvodstvennie Obejineniya' (NPOs)
attached to the regional crop research stations of RAAS.



84                                   ANNA S
Page 3 of 9
8.    There are 81 corn seed processing units in Russia, most of them (75) belong to Roskhleboprodukt
(RKP) and were built during the 60's. Most of these plants are worn-out and outdated. RAAS has 4
units and the MOAF (Federal) 2 units. RAAS units are relatively new but are not being fully utilized.
RKP organizes contract production in kolkhozes, sovkhozes and semkhozes, procures at the government
determined quota and prices, processes and distributes to farms. Considerable losses occur, in terms of
quantity and quality, both in processing units and in production fields. Processing equipments and
technology employed are outdated. Quality control at both research institutes and seed production suffer
due to lack of accountability and incentives. As a result, seeds produced are of very poor standard. The
management in dtese plants is poor and they are run without any cost recovery considerations. The
installed capacity for corn in Russia is reported in Annex Table 5.1.

9.    There are a number of joint stock (iS) seed companies besides RKP that are in the process of
becoming private in near future, e.g., Rossiskaya Semenal (RS) and some of its affiliates. Some
companies have recently registered as private joint stock companies, including KUBANGIBRID in
Krasnodar, ZOLOTOI POCHATOK of Voronezh, AZOVSKAYA SEMENA in Rostov, KADGORAN
KUKURUZA ASSOSIATSIA of North Ossetia, VOLGA GIBRID of Volgograd, CHERNOZOMIA
MASLO of Belgorod. These companies are formally established as independent companies. There are
also some kolkhozes and sovkhozes specializing in seed production which have become JS seed farms and
have formally become shareholders in the JS seed companies, as in the case of BARI seed company in
Krasnodar. These privately owned, once Govermnent-owned or quasi-government seed enterprises, are
t/Establi*ed by MOAF in 1991 as joint stock company responsible for production and maketing of seed. It is the most active seed
company at the national level amd bas 46 affliates at oblast level for organizing production and marketing of 210.000 tons of seeds.

Page 4 of 9
not able to improve their activities in terms of quantity and quality. They are unable to modernize
processing units because of the lack of access to foreign exchange to import modem equipment.
REsARCH SUPPORT TO THE SD INDUsTRY
Corn
10.   Seed research, in general, is carried out in a variety of specialized research institutes, agricultural
universities and research stations. There are 29 selection centers and 403 seed multiplication farms of the
RAAS. Most of the corn breeding program was concentrated in Dnepropetrovsky in Ukraine under the
VASKhNIL in the Former Soviet Union. Now the corn breeding program has been shifted to Krasnodar
Lukyanenko Research Institute and Nalchik, Kabardino-Balkar. The quality of corn breeding program
is mixed. Some of the research on plant breeding and genetics are of high quality, some breeding centers
are staffed with highly qualified breeders and professionals. Some of the hybrids released and area
covered is reported in Annex Table 5.2. Corn hybrid parent seeds are processed in the NPOs and
provided to farms for Fl seed production. The installed capacity at 13 crop research stations is reported
in Annex Table 5.3.

Suanfower
11.   Till recently, the Postovoit Oilseeds Development Institute at Krasnodar was a strong proponent
for open pollinated sunflower varieties. They developed excellent disease resistant germplasm but the seed
production aspects were neglected. Earlier, under FSU, scientists worked on hybrids at Odessa and
evolved some good hybrids which excel in yield levels. Now, scientists in Russia strongly believe that
a 40% increase in yield can be attained with the introduction of hybrid sunflower seeds partly because
of the heterosis and partly because of the reduction of losses facilitated by seed vigor, more uniform
growth and maturity. Recently, Cargill initiated a collaborative research program with Postovoit Institute
and has evolved two sunflower hybrids. Many companies are interested in the disease resistant
germplasm of the Postovoit Oilseeds Development Institute, and intend to sign research protocol

12.   The main problems have been the widening gap between research and its applzation, inefficient
management at production level, an isolation of scientists from advances made in rest of the world,
especially since mid seventies. Non-scientific personnel administer the production, processing, allocation
and distribution channels. importance is given to meeting specific targets for prox.lction without any
regard for technical standards, resource limitations and economic efficiency. Recent deterioration in the
economy has further worsened the situation and distanced professionals from addressing problems of
production and quality standards. Budget problems and lack of foreign exchange have severely curtailed
linkage with applied research activities.
PROJECr FEATURES
13.   The ARIS Seed Industry Development Component is designed to: (i) provide sub-loans for
establishing pilot seed enterprises for corn and sunflower seeds to demonstrate the commercial viability
of seed industry organized in the private sector; and (ii) help establish an enabling policy environment
and institutional framework for the development of competitive seed industry in the private sector. The
institutional and the policy framework aspects of the project will cover the entire country. Investments
in the seed inspection, varietal testing strengthening activity would be concentrated in the oblasts/rayons
where investment sub-projects would be implemented. The project would be confined to area where
mean annual sum of diurnal temperature is above 2800° C° during crop growth (MDT > 100 C@), in the
re,ions having comparative advantage, and where the enterprises are more active in privatization.
Investment in Seed Enterprises
14.   The project will provide loans to seed enterprises to build new seed processing facilities and
establish vertically integrated, independently operated seed companies that are market and profit oriented.
The new facilities will include technological improvements. New management structures will be instituted
at the enterprise level to improve the overall technical and financial performance of the company. These
structures include private sector management, the development of marketing structures, the establishment
of appropriate business relations with foreign seed companies to acquire access to improved germplasm,
and initial steps to begin product development (variety testing and development).
15.   The proposed investment is expected to increase the production and availability of quality seeds.
This would lead to the rapid improvement in the germplasm, production, and processing of additional
capacity of 30,000 tons of hybrid corn and 4,000 tons sunflower hybrid seeds. The seed enterprises will
be selected according to agreed criteria with the MOAF. Out of the 27 seed enterprises indicating their
interest in being included in the project, 10 enterprises initiated feasibility studies and 17 others have
indicated their intention to do so (additional companies are likely to express their desire for being
included in the project). Most of these companies had requested the assistance of the Giproselkhozerno
(GSZ) Institute in Krasnodar for carrying out feasibility studies.
Enabling Peicy Environment
16.   Institutional changes would be a key feature of this project and the MOAF would systematically
withdraw from the active seed production and distribution. This activity will build up the capacity of the
MOAF to redefine and undertake its new role. Specific emphasis will include the development of a seed
law that improves the quality of seed in the marketplace; strengthening the execution of certification
activities: improving the varietal testing and registration program; supporting adoption of plant breeder's



88                                  ANNEX S
Page 7 of 9
rights protection; systematic disengagement from production, processing and marketing of seeds; the
promotion and support of new seed enterprises in the private sector; and assistance to establish an active
national seed association of private seed entrepreneurs. Broadly, following items would be financed
under the project:
0     Strengthening of varietal testing commission (Gossortkomissia), strengthening 24 farm
trial centers, equipping them with modem precision farm machineries to enhance theit
testing efficiencies. Training would expose members of the organization to other
methods of variety testing and registration as well as enforcement of Plant Bre2deis
Rights (PBR).
0     Strengthening of sted inspection and certification system (Goseminspektsia), establishing
two central training -cum-testing centers (one at Moscow and the other at Krasnodar);
strengthening the 210 seed testing labs to enhance their efficiencies. Training would
expose mnembers of the organization to irternational methods and standards of seed
inspection and seed and variety certification. Training would also include enforcement
of Plant Breeders Rights (PBR) by members of UPOV (the international organization
assuming the leading role in PBR) and equipment training (i.e. electrophoresis). The
goal for this project would be to raise seed standards of corn and sunflower in Russia to
OECD (recognized international) levels.
O     Establishment of National Seed Advisory Council (NSAC): To provide an integrated and
rational process for defining the future role of the MOAF in the development of a
competitive seed industry based on independent, sustainable seed enterprises, it is
proposed that an advisory committee be established for the duration of the five year
project perfod. This committee will consist both of government and non-government
persons which will identify options from successful seed industry models from other
couinries and propose a national seed policy for Russia; will set goals for the orderly
transition to the MOAF new role and ensure a competitive seed industry environment
during this transition period;  will also advise on legislation and accompanying
regulations related to the implementation of the national seed policy; and meet regularly
to monitor, assess and advise the government as to how to speed up implementation of
seed industry development component of this project.
e      Formation of National Seed Association (NSA):  A non-governmental democratic
organization and MOAF will assist in its formation. NSA's members will consist of
independent seed enterprises of all sizes, seed growers, traders, corporations in Russia
involved with the production , processing, or sale of seeds and interested in working
toward a productive and sustainable agricultural environment. The NSA would represent
seed indu=rv concerns to the government. It would also keep members informed of
legislation applicable to the seed trade and the requirements of pertinent laws. The NSA
would consider and endeavor to solve problems of the seed trade. NSA would itnteract
with international seed organizations such as the Federation Internationale du Commerce
des Semences (FIS) and other national seed organizations.
17.   The project would provide assistance in the creation of the NSA, helping key people explore
successul models that exist in other countries, develop a mission statement, a prelimir.ry constitution



89                                  ANNE S
Page 8 of 9
and preliminary by-laws, and develop a campaign to attract new members. During the initial project
period, the NSA may organize educational training seminars on subjects new to Russia such as
entrepreneurship, sales, marketing, accounting procedures, dealins with bankers, dealing with the
intermational seed trade, and other topics which the membership would find useful. Linkages between
various agencies, committees, associations and departments at the federal and oblast levels are presented
in the Amex Figure 5. 1.

RUSSIAN FEDERATION
AGRICULTURAL REFORM IMPLEMENTATION SUPPORT (AIRIS) PROJECr
CRITERIA FOR SELECTiON OF PARTICIPATING PRIVATE ENTERPRISES
1.    Criteria for selection of the participating private marketing and seed enterprises for the sub-loan
program are as follows:
(i)    The enterprises should have completed the privatization process (as per GKI guidelines).
(ii)    The enterprise management will be independent (not controlled by the govermnent),
vested with day-to-day decision-making authority, profit oriented, and accountable to the
Board of Directors.
(iii)   Enterprises mdst be in satisfactory financial condition (need audited financial statements
and balance sheets).
(iv)   The existing and potential profitability of an enterprise must be acceptable to the Bank.
(v)    Enterprises must agree to employ technically trained managers to manage new
investment.
(vi)   Enterprises must complete feasibility studies for the proposed sub-projects which are
acceptable to PDU, MOAF and the World Bank.
(vii)   The participating private enterprises must be in a position to contribute 15-35 percent of
the total cost of the sub-project and pay necessary duties and taxes, including VAT.
(viii)  The enterprise must sign a subsidiary loan agreement stipulating the terms of the loan,
procurement and repayment procedures, reporting and project monitoring, security
arrangements, accounting and financial covenants.
(ix)   The fruit and vegetable farms must adopt a production restructuring plan to improve
production and productivity to ensure financial viability of the proposed investment.
(x)    The seed enterprises must have experience in the seed sector and must meet
criteria for ownership, access to genetic resources, geographic location, and
financial audits.
2.    Additional eligibility criteria may be added during implementation as the Government and
the World Bank acquire more experience in on-lending to private enterprises.

RUSSIAN 1FEDERATION
AGRICULTURAL REFORM IMPLEMENTATION SUPPORT (AIS) ]PROJECT
TRAINING MODULE
JUSTIFICATION
1.    The success of the ARIS project depends on the timely availability of trained manpower to
undertake diverse activitiks envisaged in the project. Tht principle objective of training is to provide
relevant technical and managerial skills to a large number of personnel who would be responsible for tue
implementation of individual project components.
2.    The total training package of about US$14.2 million for the entire ARIS project spread over a
period of five years has been developed in consultation with the various component Working Groups in
the Ministry of Agriculture and Food and with the relevant agencies and enterprises. Th12- main
justification for training is that the project requires new types of skills and experience as many of the
project activities require new approaches, which are quite different from those being practiced at the
present time in Russia. The main emphasis of the training package, therefore, is to provide these
necessary practical skills in a variety of disciplines to those involved with the implementation of the
project, as well as to expected project beneficiaries. A large number of persons drawn from different
agencies, departnents, government institutions from the federal, oblast and rayon levels, private
enterprises and from different farm structures would benefit from this training.
3.    Given the broad range of activities being carried out by each of the project components, it
requires different types of training for persons with varying backgrounds at different locations and times
of project execution. Broadly, the project will support two types of training, viz., (i) in-country and (ii)
foreign. The duration of training ranges from short one to five day workshops to extended programs of
one month or even longer. This traimng module provides a brief description of the various types of
training programs that the ARIS project would support for each of the project components.
MAREE INFRASUCrURE DEVELOPENT  -
Mket Infonnaion System (M
4.    The objective of the MIS training is to develop the sldlls of the MOAF staff in modem methods
of market information collection, analysis, preparation and dissemination. MIS training will cover two
broad areas: (i) collection, processing and dissemination of market information and (ii) computer
hardware and applications development.



93                                  ANNEX 7
Page 2 of 6
5.    In-country Training: (i) Data processing methods: About 1200 MOAF staff from the oblast and
rayon levels will be trained over a three year period in data collection, interviewing techniques, data
processing and consolidation, grades and standards, preparation of information releases and computer
operations. In addition, manuals for MIS activities will be prepared. (ii) Technical Computer Training:
Since the ARIS computer system would be a complex system comprising 1500 nodes, in-country training
for about 100 computer specialists would be provided in three broad areas: system architects, UNIX
system design, Distributed Computing Environment, Object oriented application development. In addition,
specialized short term courses will be developed for computer systems analysts of the rayon and oblast
levels. These will focus on programming languages, network design, application upgrading and security
administration. (iii) Hands on Training Computer Workshops: Since majority of the data that would
flow through the ARIS network originates at the farm level, about 1000 short hands-on training
workshops at the end-user level will be conducted by MOAFCC. These will focus on overview of the
ARIS computer network, how it operates, overview of applications, how the MIS and FIAS information
is collected and disseminated, what is required to access the system and what benefits it can offer.
6.    Foreign Training: (i) International Experience: Ten higher and middle level staff would
undertake short tours to selected foreign countries to observe the operations of market information
systems. (ii) Computer Network design: The ARIS computer network system involves the use of the
latest hardware and software technology. This network will be used by the MIS and FIAS for providing
market and farmer information, respectively. Five senior officials engaged in the operations of the
computer network would be trained in selected foreign countries for about six months in various technical
and manag-,ment aspects of modem computer network design and operations. (iii) Software applications:
Officials engaged in the development of specialized software applications would be provided with specific
traming in specialized computer software languages and application oriented languages in selected foreign
countries. Ten individuals would be provided with this training.
Market Enterprise Development
7.    The training programs is designed to complement the activities being undertaken by the Market
Infrastructure Development component. This would involve the training of appropriate MOAF officials
at the federal and regional levels. Through this process, the concerned officials would be equipped with
thc necessary skills and exposure to carry out the intended activities of the project.
8.    In-country Training: This would consists of a number of short training programs for MOAF
officials, regional authorities, promoters of primary and wholesale markets, managers and functionaries
in market organizations. Over 2000 persons are expected to undergo this training. The subject areas
would be: institutional aspects of marketing, different types of market infrastructure, trading practices,
grades and standards and the role of wholesale markets in the distribution system for agricultural
products.
9.    Foreign Training: About 30 officials from federal and oblast level governments, marketing
organizations and training institutes will visit major marketing systems in selected countries in Europe
and North America.



94                                   ANNEX 7
Page 3 of 6
FARMER INFORMATION AND ADVISORY SERVICES
10.   The main objectives of training in the Farmer Information and Advisory Services Component are
two-fold: to enhance the knowledge and skills of a large number of FIAS staff and end-users in specific
skill areas; and to provide first hand exposure to various methods of farmer information development and
dissemination outside the Russian Federation.
Farmer Information Development
11.   In-Country Training: A variety of short training programs will be undertaken for about 350
FIAS staff from the federal, oblast and rayon levels. These training programs would focus on: (i)
information needs assessment, including new methods of information needs assessment such as critical
success factors method (CSF), spot surveys, feed-back mechanisms; (ii) information sourcing and message
development, message packaging for multi-media; (iii) quick data collection designs, data analysis, data
presentation; (iv) development and preparation of easy to understand and easy to use manuals for farm
management, business, technical packages, marketing; (v) development of computer databases and expert
systems for ongoing reference; and (vi) development of user friendly environmental, technical and legal
data base.
12.   Periodic two to three day workshops on agricultural information, marketing and business skills
development will be held at the rayon, oblast and federal levels. These will be specially designed for
about 6500 end-users during the five year project period representing a wide range of project
beneficiaries, from the emerging small independent farmer to large re-structured farir. and agri-business
enterprises. The training will be provided by foreign and local experts. Specialized training programs
would be developed for training of trainers.
13.   Foreign Training: The local training will be supplemented by specialized study tours of about
thmee to four weeks for about 200 senior and middle management Russian experts from the federal,
oblast, rayon offices and about 500 representatives of the various end-users to selected countries and
observe first hand the workings of: (i) agricultural extension systems and how they operate in different
countries, (ii) structure and planning of the extension system and its interaction with agricultural research,
(iii) information sources and role of the private sector; (iv) operations of the local farm level extension
offices, (v) basic farm management tools, farm accounts, farm budgets and cost analysis; (vi) provision
of technical advice for specific crops and livestock activities, and various technical subject matters, (vii)
organizations and operations of farmer organizations, producers associations and cooperatives, (viii)
provide hands-on experience of information flows and use in agro-business operations including those
providing farm inputs, storage and handling farm products, processing and farm credit.
Farmer Information Dissemination
14.   In-Country Training: Short training programs will be undertaken for about 300 personnel from
ARSRIIMA, AKKOR and the Video Center of the Ministry of Agriculture and Food. These training
programs would focus on instructional design, modem production techniques for television, radio, print
and video productions, multimedia information dissemination techniques, cost benefit analysis of different
media selection, and interactive video techniques for different client groups. The training will be provided
by foreign and local experts. Specialized training programs would be developed for training of trainers.



95                                   ANNEX 7
Page 4 of 6
15.   Foreign Training: The local training will be supplemented by foreign training programs of about
three to four weeks in specialized information dissemination techniques for about S0 operational staff,
from AKKOR, ARSRIIMA and MOAF's Video Center. Special programs dealing with relevant
international farming and agro-industrial practices will also be produced by Russian teams for
dissemination through video, radio and television.
SEED INDUSRY DEVELoPMENT
16.   The objective of the training component is to provide: (i) the participating private seed enterprises
with the needed business and marketing skills to operate in a commercial environment, and (ii) expose
the key policy makers in the MOAF and NSAC members to regulatory aspects of seed industry as
practiced in market economies and improve the quality control, varietal testing and standard setting
functions of the operational field staff of Gossemispektsia and Gossortkomisia.
Private Seed Enterprises
17.   In-Country Training: Management of private seed enterprises: The training programs are aimed
at senior management and financial officers of the participating private sector. They will undergo in-
county courses and seminars in accounting, financial management, investment analysis, seed production
and seed processing. The officials in charge of finance and accounting would undertake two courses in
activity-based accounting, four training events in contract grower management and other technical topics,
and three seminars to cover strategic planning, project identification, project prioritization, the parameters
for feasibility studies, and the evaluation of feasibility documents. The training will be provided by the
long-term consultants working in the PDU. Counterpart staff and other experts will be trained through
on-the-job training, workshops, seminars and the step-by-step development of a project preparation
manual.
18.   Strategic Project Planning and Projer' Preparation: Workshops and Seminars on the subjects of
strategic planning, project identification, project prioritization, the parameters for feasibility studies, and
the evaluation of feasibility documents will be undertaken annually during the first 3 years of project
implementation. These workshops will include presentations on the activities of the seed investment sub-
component. Both government and private sector participants will be invited to the workshops. Foreign
companies interested in establishing operations in Russia will be strongly encouraged to participate.
Three foreign consultants will give presentations and coordinate the program activities, and will also
prepare a Project Preparation Manual. Inputs into the manual will come from the workshops, the training
modules for the counterpart staff, the seminars, and other relevant sources such as the MOAF, EBRD,
EU and other World Bank staff.
19.   Foreign Training: (i) Management of private seed enterprises: Senior management of the
participating seed enterprises will be trained in improving their management skills, preparation of
investment proposals and analysis. This will be achieved through study tours to selected foreign seed
enterprises, Secondary topics related to the operation of the contract grower program, as well as
processing and packaging, can be included where appropriate. The participants would visit three on-going
seed enterprises that will be selected to provide the maximum exposure to the issues involved.
(ii) Financial management and marketing aspects: The financial and marketing officials of the private seed
enterprises would visit on-going seed enterprises and study the management and marketing aspects of the
seed business.

Foreign Training:
21.   National Seed Advisory Committee (NSAC) : As the NSAC will be providing leadership for

established in seed industries of successful western .ountries with differing systems. Training for ten
Russian specialists (who will be resource persons to train the local staff as trainers) will be provided for
about a month in a selected foreign country to study laboratory techniques and methods for enforcement

of the seed law, with special emphasis on enforcement of varietal purity ana plant breeders' rights. These

RUSSIAN FEDERATION
AGRICULTURAL REFORM IMPLEMENTATION SUPPORT (ARIS) PROJECT
Technical Assistance Module
JUSTIFICAION
1.    The objectives of technical assistance for the ARIS project are to provide specialized assistance
in a variety of specific skill areas needed for the speedy implementation of project zomponents and sub-
components. The total technical assistance package of US$10.4 million for the ARIS project spread over
five years has been developed in close consultation with the various component Working Groups in the
Ministry of Agriculture and Food and with the relevant regional administrations. The main emphasis of
the overall package is to provide the most critically needed skills and expertise in selected areas which
are presently unavailable in the participating institutions in the Russian Federation and, where possible,
transfer these skills to Russian counterparts assigned to work with the foreign experts.
DELivEY OF TECHICAL AssISANcE
2.    Given the diverse set of activities requiring different expertise over both time and space in the
ARIS project, the delivery of the technical assistance package will be carried out in three ways: (i) long-
term individual services from one to three years; (ii) short-term individual or firm services for six months
or less to be provided at critical time intervals; and (iii) task oriented services requiring multi-disciplinary
teams. Provision of technical assistance services would be subject to World Bank review and clearance.
The resource requirements, phasing and skill areas are provided in the Annex Table 8.1. The indicative
TORs, which are subject to modifications during the implementation of the project, are provided below
for each component of the ARIS project. All TORs will require a prior review by the Bankl and be
supplemented by implementation review during the supervision missions. All the reports prepared by
the technical assistance staff will be jointly reviewed by the PDU and the World Bank.
TORs FOR MARKEr INnwsArRucruRE DEVELOPMENT
3.    The technical assistance in this component has been designed to provide specific skills to the
MOAF for the implementation of: (1) market information system and (2) development of marketing

(ii)   Task Two: Primary and Wholesale Market Development
Location of Assignment: Seven economic regions in the Russian Federation
Duration of the assignment
(a)    Phase 1: September 1994 to July 1995

(a) Phase 1:  (i) review of current laws, rules and regulations at the federal and oblast level
concerning the establishment and management of primary and wholesale markets
and MOAF's concept paper on formation of organized markets in the agro-
industrial sector;
(ii) assess the adequacy of these regulations for a competitive development of
primary and wholesale markets;
(iii) develop institutional arrangements for market organization and management
using oblast and MOAF guidelines; and
(iv) assist MOAF to determine the potential for development of such markets in
twenty selected oblasts
(b) Phase 2:  (i) review proposals for market development in 20 oblasts and select 10 proposals
based on agreed criteria;
(ii) carry out ten techno-economic feasibility studies of selected critical
investments; and
(ii) develop packages appropriate for financing such investments fxom dAomestic
and international resources.

RUSSIAN FEDERATION
AGRICULTURAL REFORM IPLEMENTATION SUPPORT (AIS) PROJECT
DETAILED PROJECT AND COMPONENT COSTS
The detailed costs for individual project components and cost categories are summarized in Annex
Tables 9.1 to 9.6 of this Annex. The base cost estimates were derived by the mission, in consultation
with MOAF counterparts, from feasibility studies, surveys and preparation reports. All costs were
expressed in US dollars. The underlying assumptions are as follows:
(a)    Physical Contingencies:           10 percent for civil works and equipment and
machinery (base costs) applied to all costs
expressed in US dollars, in line with established
Bank practice and experience with similar
projects worlewide.
(b)    Price Contingencies:              2.8 percent per annum (compounded) for civil
works and equipment and machinery (base costs
+ physical contingencies) and 2.8 percent
(compounded) for operating cost, training and
technical assistance (base costs) were applied to
all costs expressed in US dollars (according to
the average annual price increases projected by
the World Bank between 1992 and 2(C02).
(c)    Import Duties:                   15 percent of the estimated CIF cost for the
equipment and machinery.  Import duties
continue to change and 15 percent is about an
average.    Furthermore, Govermnent has
indicated its intention to re-examine the
structure of import duties in the near future.
(d)    VAT:                             23 percent of the estimated CIF cost for the
imported equipment and machinery (not
included in the cost tables).  Regulations
governing the levying of VAT on imports and
how it might be expensed against the capital
expenditure is under review.
